B0000A1RJI|4|When I first saw the theatrical trailers for this film, I was excited.  Being a huge Disneyland fan, I was naturally enthralled by the idea of a movie based on one of the park's most innovative and successful rides.  The music in the trailer somewhat confused me, though.  The lively \\"Yo-Ho\\" theme used in the ride couldn't be heard--instead, I heard driving orchestral music that sounded different from anything I'd heard before.  But I liked it a lot, and began trying to arrange it for piano. <br /> <br />Fast forward a few months.  I saw the film and really enjoyed it.  The music caught my attention again--it was very, very similar to what I'd heard in the trailer, but it wasn't exactly the same.  Nevertheless, I knew I needed the soundtrack. <br /> <br />Now, a few years later, I have most of the 45-minute soundtrack arranged for solo piano and play it regularly.  The soundtrack itself is a well-loved addition to my iPod's hard drive, and I know others who enjoy it as well.  Interestingly, this score works so well because it is NOT stereotypical \\"pirate music.\\"  The film is by no means a conventional pirate film, and Klaus Badelt's take on the music is intriguingly modern.  It mixes orchestral and electronic elements into a sonic texture that Hans Zimmer's Media Ventures has made so ubiquitous in films of this nature. <br /> <br />If you're looking for a fresh and unique approach to film scoring, POTC is not for you.  This is the same sort of music that Zimmer and Badelt and the other composers at Media Ventures have written for films like The Time Machine and Gladiator.  That being said, this is of somewhat higher caliber than other Media Ventures scores I've heard. <br /> <br />Several very similar themes are utilized throughout the score.  Sometimes they become rather monotonous, but there are some renditions that are shockingly moving.  \\"One Last Shot\\" is the most unique track on the album, featuring an incredibly passionate statement of the main love theme, aswell as a number of French horn \\"echoes\\" of the other themes in the movie. <br /> <br />Let me sum up what I intended to say in this overly long review: <br /> <br />This is neither pure orchestral music nor pure electronic music.  The three or four very similar themes that Badelt composed for the film are used in a number of contexts, sometimes monotonously.  However, every track has its strong points.  Much of the music is loud and uses driving rhythmic figures. <br /> <br />Now we'll have to see how Zimmer does on his score for the film's sequel.  Only time will tell.

B00M2D7L2I|3|Is it as good as the first two 5 star albums? To me it's 3.5 stars. I'm sure some fans are pxssed at this question because it's not fair. But for a lot of people this is the question they want answered. This is the question many old fans will be asking, this review is for you, not everyone and not for fans of Weezer's newer stuff. This is simply a review for people who have not yet bought the album and are wondering if it's as good as Blue and Pinkerton. This is for fans who just love the first 2 and didn't really care for all their other albums. This review will try to judge from a \\"how accessible is it?\\" stand point of view. Please don't vote yes or no unless you're an older fan from the early 90s wanting to know if this album is as good as the first 2, it wasn't intended for everyone else.    On some levels it is and some it isn't. The new album lacks the gritty, raw, enthusiastic energy of the first 2, the production is much cleaner on the new album. The vocals, guitars, and drums don't have the same intense energy as the first 2, I'm sure it has to do with them aging, gaining fame, popularity through the years which is normal and expected. The emotions of the singing combined with the juvenile lyrics feel contrived to some degree, like an older Rivers trying to capture the emotions of youth, it doesn't feel completely real to a degree. But the lyrics match their first 2, it just feels more contrived now being older with less singing emotion. After 8 good listens, some of the middle tracks do lose my attention, bored me a bit, and felt meaningless, my mind wandered.    The album isn't at all bad, it's the same weezer, just less energetic (compared to the first 2). No real change, artistic innovation was really made on this album either, so it's not a far departure from the first 2, nor is it a experimental artistic statement piece. The production is clean, tight, and songwriting is good. Many are saying this album is as good as the first 2, some riffs, lyrics, and sounds comes close but just lacks the gritty energy. Maybe if it were recorded live, it would be closer to the first 2. But this album definitely is better than some of the later weezer albums. So it's not the best, nor the worst. The hooks of this album doesn't hook you like the first 2, but the hooks are still good. The only song I didn't like was one with hipster whistling in it.    Here you have a really good weezer album, things changed as expected, but not a life changer like the first 2. Good songwriting, good riffs, ok energy, good hooks, decent emotional impact. So if you don't care about the gritty, enthusiastic energy of the first 2, you may find this album just as good as their first. Basically, If you take the their debut self titled blue album and Pinkerton and polished away the raw in your face energy and took away some of the catchy hooks and lowered their emotional impact and the realness of the lyrics and add nothing new you'd have Everything Will be Alright in the End. It's still pretty good, just lacks the magic of the first 2.    Here's an example comparison of other bands and artists changing equivalence of Weezers \\"Blue album and Pinkerton vs Everything Will be Alright in the End\\" is like:    Led Zeppelin's I -IV and Houses of the Holy vs Coda and physical graffiti.  Black Sabbath's Debut and Paranoid vs 13.  Nine inch nails Pretty hate machine, downward spiral, fragile vs hesitation marks.  Godsmack's debut vs 1000 hp.  Disturbs the Sickness vs Asylum.  Bjork's debut, post, homogenic, and vespertine vs Medulla, Volta, and Biophelia.  Metallica's Ride the lightning and master of puppets vs black album and death magnetic.  Jimmy eat worlds Clarity vs Invented or Bleed American.  Pink Floyd's Wish you were here, The Wall, and Dark Side of The Moon vs momentary lapse of reason.  The Doors debut vs the la woman.  Deftones adrenaline, around the fur, and White Pony vs Saturday night wrist.  Pearl Jams 10 vs Backspacer.  Guns and roses appetite for destruction vs Chinese democracy and use your illusion.  The clash's debut vs give them the rope.  Rancid's Out came the wolves vs Life won't wait.  Fleetwood Mac's Rumours vs Say you will.  Martin Scorsese's taxi driver and goodfellas vs the departed and aviator.  Stephen Spielberg's E.T. Vs A.I.  Michael Mann's Heat vs Public Enemies.  Star Wars original vs new trilogy.  Pulp Fiction vs Django Unchained.  Indiana jones original trilogy vs the 4th movie.  Mudhoney's super fuzz big muff vs all their other releases.  Sarah Mclachlan's Fumbling towards ecstasy and surfacing vs Laws of Illusion and shine on.  David Bowie's rise and fall of ziggy stardust vs the next day.    This is just an example comparison. I don't think any of the later releases by the artists mentioned are bad, just a lesser or different emotional impact like Weezer's Everything Will be Alright in the End. Artists change and it's ok sometimes. Some will even find the later stuff better or just as good.

B0054N73EY|4|You guys believe it? It's been more than 5 years since the Chilis released Stadium... The wait for new material from my favourite band has been a long one, to say the least.    The day I heard Frusciante decided to leave the Chilis was a devastating blow to me. It was a sad time for me and a lot of Chili Peppers fans alike. I got through it though, accepting the fact that John was passed the rock band stage in his life and wanted to focus on creating his own stuff. It made it easier for me to accept knowing that he left on good terms and that he was truly happy with the decision.     I don't know where I heard it from, but the Chilis acknowledged they were a completely brand new band, except for the fact that they just kept the name... I first listened to the album when they streamed it online. Yesterday, on the first day of release, I drove like a madman during my lunch break from work and bought the album (I haven't bought an actual CD in ages). I wanted to write about this earlier but I thought, the least I could do is give it a real good listen before I began to critique it. One has to understand that this is the follow up to Stadium Arcadium, pretty much a 'perfect' album in every sense.    My overall feel for the album is pretty good. I already knew going into it that I was not going to get the same feeling I would from a Frusci chilied album... I mean, Frusci lives to play music. His passion, devotion, and love for music is so strong, its an inspiration to see how in tune somebody can be with something... Comparing Josh to Frusci can't be done fairly because we all know Frusci is simply put, irreplaceable.    The album seemed very chills to me, which is what the Chilis bring, so I thought Josh did a great job on keeping that Chilis feel. But you're also missing a lot of the funk, something John started off in with and went through this amazing evolution over the years...Chad is solid like he always is. Flea always outdoes himself but is always a bit underrated, and Kiedis keeps getting better and better, vocally over the years. All of the instruments we're not normally used to (the ever increasing piano, the good ol' trumpet from flea, African drums, and even the cow bell) from the Chilis gives them a fresh sound, which is refreshing.    Now, if you HAD to make a comparison, you can compare Josh with Navarro, as they both came in after Frusciante leaves (both incredibly successful albums), whether on good terms or not. One Hot Minute had some good songs, but I can already say I like 'I'm With You' better. There are some real outstanding songs on the album which I've been playing over and over. If I had to say my top 5, here they are, not in any particular order:    3. Brendan's Death Song  8. Did I Let You Know   10. Happiness Loves Company   11. Police Station   13. Meet Me at the Corner     I think speaking for a lot of Chilis fans, we can all agree that we miss John's harmonizing and his solos... Frusci lets it all out with his solos, he makes you feel his emotions and his soul through them. (Jaddo, you know all of them amazing solos, way too many to name.) These are the huge things that's missing from this album. Josh does bring in some good vocals to the album however. I'm not trying to be biased at all here, but it still comes out a little bit. It sort of feels like Josh is holding back, rather, choosing to compliment the other 3 more than showcasing himself. Nonetheless, Josh is a great fit with the band. He's the natural person to step in after John leaves because of their closeness, and just the fact that he truly understands what the band is about.    Overall, the album is very good. It's very good, but not the same as the old stuff and it will never be that way because Josh is Josh, and John is John. Do I recommend it? Yes, go buy it for the love of Chilis whether you are a long time fan or whether you're just starting to realize the magic and universal love they exude.    Here's how I've always looked at them. Chad is like the rock of the group; Kiedis is the ball of energy or the flame; Flea is the crazy glue that holds the band in place; and Frusci... Frusci is the heart of the band. The Chilis just got a heart transplant and they're still going strong.

0385491026|3|Margaret Atwood once wrote, &quot;Sisterhood is powerful; women are always supposed to get along with each other.  It's not true any more than it is for men.&quot;  Cat's Eye is basically about jealousy and cruelty between girls, as remembered by Elaine, now an adult, who has returned to her  hometown to visit.  As Elaine is walking through the city, she remembers  scenes that are each centered on a specific theme.  Some of these topics  include victimization, cultural dislocation, power struggles and violence  against females.  Atwood's main theme explores how girls can be fiercely  competitive and very cruel.  Atwood makes it clear that girls are not made  of &quot;sugar and spice and everything nice&quot;.  In one scene,  Cordelia, the leader of the group of girls who torment Elaine, throws  Elaine's hat into an icy cold stream and orders her to fetch it, and in  turn, almost kills her.  In the end, Elaine rises above her tormentors and  becomes more socially acceptable than her so-called friends.  During her  high school years, Cordelia actually tries to befriend her, but Elaine  holds control over her now.  The last half of the book is then devoted to  her life beyond her cruel friends, and also to her guilt for not helping  Cordelia.  Although this may seem like a fun and exciting plot to some, the  intense descriptive language is actually somewhat disturbing.  Atwood  vividly describes incidences such as Elaine peeling layers of skin off her  feet and also how she feels while having sex.  I gave it three stars  because although Cat's Eye is very long and disturbing, I thought that  Atwood incorporated some surprisingly true statements that I had never  thought of before.  I was surprised at how much I related to some of these  statements, like pain keeping people in reality.  Cat's Eye is very lengthy  and at times monotonous, but I actually like it now that I've finished  reading it.

B00005J6T1|5|Madonna debuted with this record in late 1983, initiating the most successful female pop career in history.  At the time, disco was dead and dance music was verboten on pop radio.  Along with Shannon, Madonna helped bring dance music back into the mainstream.  Thus, although \\"Madonna\\" sounds like safe pop music now, it was actually pretty cutting edge at the time.  \\"Everybody\\" was her first single; it became a solid dance hit but didn't cross over to pop radio or the Hot 100.  With its unusual shuffling beat, it should have been a hit and still sounds great today.<br /><br />\\"Madonna\\" eventually yielded three pop hits, each one charting higher then the previous - Holiday (#16), Borderline (#10), and Lucky Star (#4).  \\"Borderline\\" was her first ballad, although relatively up-tempo.  Her voice is thinner here than it would be on later ballads, but she still sounds lovely.  The video was also a huge hit and introduced people to Madonna's breakthrough style.  I became aware of Madonna for the first time through that video and have been a fan ever since.  \\"Lucky Star\\" sounds a bit dated with too many synthesizers, although it's still a great pop song.  Although \\"Holiday\\" was the smallest hit, it's perhaps the most enduring of the three: a real party anthem.<br /><br />Along with these hits, the non-singles are also uniformly solid.  \\"Burning Up\\" is the closest thing to a rock song that Madonna made during her early years, although the guitars are paired with a terrific dance beat.  \\"Physical Attraction\\" is another highlight - a dance song that really shows off Madonna's sex appeal and slither.  \\"Think of Me\\" and \\"I Know It\\" are the two least memorable songs on this CD - straight ahead dance tunes without much of Madonna's panache.  With just 8 songs, \\"Madonna\\" breezes by quickly and sometimes seems a bit insubstantial.  However, the CD is an undeniable dance classic that began the Queen of Pop's career.  Most highly recommended.

B000JSI7AI|5|When I first saw Brokeback with my two best friends, I was about fourteen years old. All three of us appreciated it and were torn by the ending, (especially my friend who spent most of the movie gushing over Jake Gyllenhaal) but I didn't give it a whole lot of thought until a few months ago when I realized how powerful a film it really is. I borrowed it from my friend and watched it and it instantly re-captivated me.    I watched it about three times in one week, noticing new symbolism and meaning each time in the phrases and actions of the characters. I noticed that the looks Jack and Ennis give one another when they first begin herding together are more than just obligatory. After reading Roger Ebert's helpful and honest review, I realized that Ennis really was taught to hate himself from an early age because of his upbringing. Some Japanese amazon reviews taught me to see that, when Ennis first finds his and Jack's shirts, Jack's is embracing Ennis', whereas at the end of the film, Ennis has his own shirt embracing Jack's. One thing I noticed on my own was that, (however obvious it might have been to others who have seen the film it took me a while to get it...) in the scene where Ennis is longingly holding the intertwined shirts, he is, 'in the closet', so to speak.    This is not to say that I have reached a 'conclusion' as to whether Jack and Ennis were gay, bi or straight. I simply don't believe they need to be labeled as anything for that could very well distract from what this film really is about ~ genuine love. The harshness, cruelty and unforgiving-ness of society has crippled many, and Jack and Ennis are no exception. Taking into account their upbringing and environment, theirs was a love that never would have made sense to anyone around them, including Ennis himself. Though they may have cheated on their wives, they were cheated first by society out of what could have been an everlasting happiness. I have now realized that Ennis fell in love with Jacknot because he was gay or straight, but because it was Jack. Jack entered Ennis' life like a gust of wind and left just as abruptly and was the only true love Ennis would ever experience. It's just a shame Ennis was unable to escape his past and the way he was taught.

0553801473|5|I loved reading A Dance with Dragons, but I certainly did not always enjoy it. In fact, certain parts of the book are so dark they defy the imagination. Defenders of the darkness of the A Song of Ice and Fire series have often compared the books' grittiness to the evil of our own reality. But the world that sprang forth from the mind George R. R. Martin is perhaps even darker than our own miserable planet. Various parts of the book brought forth to mind the horrors of events such as the pestilence of the Black Death, or the cannibalistic doom of the Donner Party, or the psychopathic serial killer Robert Hansen. Seemingly all of the misery that human minds can recall from our wretched history has been marshaled into this single tome.<br /><br />Fans of George R.R. Martin's entire oeuvre will recognize that Martin's hallmark is a fascination with broken, corrupt, and decaying worlds. Throughout his fiction are found worlds that have once tasted grandeur, but have rotted away through the efforts of both time and humanity. The world of A Song of Ice and Fire is no different. Its lands are filled with ruined cities, extinct civilizations, and scattered peoples who squabble over memories.<br /><br />Perhaps it is fair that some question why these books should even be called fantasy when they might just as well be labeled as horror? Some of the passages from A Dance with Dragons are far more horrific than anything Hollywood has produced, perhaps ever. But I totally disagree with the notion that fantasy cannot be horrific as well. Too long have we suffered fantasy literature that dwells endlessly in shining castles. Soon enough, the grand castles, gleaming swords, and sage wizards become bland without some truly horrific stuff to spice it all up. Martin provides us with the spices we all crave. They may burn our mouths when we eat them, but once we have tasted them, we crave them. Not everyone can handle spicy food, and not everyone can handle fantasy books filled to the brim with rape, torture, mutilation, cannibalism, and all the other unpleasantries of life.<br /><br />Even if it can be a little dark, A Dance with Dragons is definitely the most magical and fantastical of the books so far. Bran's portion of the story alone was wonderful to read and would probably have made for a great children's fantasy if not for all the the violence. With the return of dragons to the world, magic and sorcery have been let loose, but never do they overwhelm the human elements of the story. Even the sorceress Melisandre misinterprets her visions and resort to cheap tricks to fool her audience.<br /><br />Another valid criticism of A Dance with Dragons might be that it is not as tightly wound as the first three books were. But it is a criticism that is only valid if one does not consider the narrative structure of the series as a whole. The series began with almost every character of note gathered at Winterfell. Through the many infamous twists and turn of the books, the story has become shattered like a crystal vase smashed into the ground. One cannot give readers so much thrilling death and destruction as Martin did in the first three books without breaking a lot of vases. But what death caused, death can also cure. Many smaller characters died off in A Dance with Dragons, and the pace will probably accelerate through The Winds of Winter.<br /><br />It is valuable to remember that Martin has always loved telling short stories set in his broken worlds. And he could not resist inserting some small stories for secondary characters into A Feast for Crows and A Dance with Dragons. The skeptic will use these as evidence that Martin has \\"lost control of his narrative.\\" I prefer to describe this tendency as \\"just plain awesome.\\" The Chicago Sun-Times once said that A Game of Thrones is \\"an absorbing combination of the mythic, the sweepingly historical, and the intensely personal.\\" Where A Feast for Crows was abound with the personal, it lacked the epic portion of the formula. A Dance with Dragons made the personal stories epic in and of themselves.<br /><br />The book isn't perfect. Martin uses some phrases and words too freely and repetitively. I don't think we've seen the words niello, neeps, or serjeant before in the series, but they show up again and again throughout the book in multiple diverse contexts. The inner thoughts of many characters consists of the same phrases repeated many times over. It's effective but definitely not subtle.<br /><br />To be sure, those who scoff at the old chestnut that \\"The journey is more important than the destination\\" will surely dislike this book. A Song of Ice and Fire is in many ways like the river journey of Tyrion Lannister or that of Abner Marsh in Martin's own Fevre Dream or that of Charles Marlow in Joseph Conrad's Heart of Darkness. That is to say, it is a journey into the darkness of the human soul. A Dance with Dragons is but a leg of that journey, offering scant resolution, but heaps of oppressive doom. The coming winter described so vividly in the novel is but a reflection of the descent of the humans of the novel into a self-imposed hell of hatred, fear, hunger, and death.<br /><br />Those hoping for more resolution in The Winds of Winter may get some, but those hoping for some light at the end of the tunnel will be sorely disappointed, just as they were very likely disappointed in this book. This story can only grow even darker as winter comes in all its fury. I predict that those squeamish of reading about cannibalism will be made ill by the next book. We all know Martin loves detailed descriptions of foodstuffs, and eating each other seems to be the only hope of making it to A Dream of Spring for many of the people of Westeros. How do wights' livers taste? Probably not too bad with some neeps and a nice Arbor red.

Even during his time with Genesis, I don't think he got the credit he deserved for his guitar work - truly a virtuoso player with a unique and original style, yet understated. A lot of his playing back then was almost subliminal. Maybe why he didn't get the notoriety he rightfully deserved? I can't think of any other guitarist, along with Alan Holdsworth, who have this much talent, and yet remain relatively unknown for the most part, even by other guitarists.<br /><br />As for this CD - I originally bought this CD back in the mid 90's while I was looking for one of Hackett's classical CDs (Midsummer Night's Dream also a phenom disc - pick it up when you have the chance). I looked at this track listing and saw that he was basically offering re-worked, re-recorded versions of some of the great old Genesis music. This immediately struck a chord with me but for no other reason then just to answer a question that I've been asking myself for the past 25 or so years - when I listen to many of my old great favorite albums of the 60s and 70s (particularly the Prog/Art Rock ones) I find myself always wondering what these recordings would sound like if done today, in our modern recording studios. Well Steve has gone ahead and answered that question for me, at least as far as a few of Genesis' songs are concerned, and the results are astounding.<br /><br />The lineup of musicians he has put together for this project is also very noteworthy. And they do NOT disappoint. John Wetton sounds as though he's been singing these songs all his life. And Hackett's playing? - NO MORE understated guitar here. H efinally pulls out all the stops and shows once and for all that he belongs at the top amongst any of the other guitar greats.<br /><br />One can only hope that sometime in the future He will do a follow up to this CD with a few more \\"re-awakenings\\" of the early Gensis stuff. My own personal wish list:<br /><br />Suppers Ready (with Gabriel doing the \\"guest\\" vocal)<br />Get `em out by Friday (with John Wetton)<br />Cinema Show<br />Robbery, Assault and Battery<br />Squonk<br />For Absent Friendsometime in the future He will do a follow up to this CD with a few more \\"re-awakenings\\" of the early Gensis stuff. This book is basically devoted to describe how we would react the day we understand that we are not alone, both politically and religiously. B002ZG97RY|5|One of the most common complaints I've read about this film is the \\"liberal agenda\\" that this film represents. I didn't know that the search for truth is exclusively a \\"liberal agenda\\" and the \\"Hollywood Elite\\" is only interested in slamming the Bush Administration and not exploring other ideas and creating solid art. Why is that such a knee-jerk reaction over films of this element? If this were an \\"anti-Obama\\" or \\"anti-Clinton\\" film, would these same people be making these claims? Of course not. I believe that time will out and this film may very well be regarded as a great film, as it should already be.<br /><br />When I first heard of Matt Damon and Paul Greengrass reteaming for a film about the current Iraq war, I was very excited since I am a HUGE fan of their previous work together. THE BOURNE SUPREMACY/ULTIMATUM are two extraordinary pieces of action filmmaking and represent the best that the techno spy thriller genre has to offer. Later hearing that it was based on a true story about the search for WMD at the beginning of the Iraq war, I was even more interested to see how Greengrass would handle such a subject. After all, Greengrass, as a filmmaker, is no stranger to the territory of this subject matter, namely the great and tragic docudrama UNITED 93.<br /><br />So while we follow Chief Warrant Officer Roy Miller's (Damon, excellent as per usual) quest to find WMD and find why he keeps coming up snake-eyes for all of his and his team's efforts, and why he keeps finding himself out of the loop between the Army, the Department of Defense, and the CIA keeping him in the dark while people are dying. The film turns from Iraq War film to mystery/thriller as Miller finds himself searching for a top-secret contact code-named Magellan, who is the person providing the misleading intel about the WMD. He finds himself either paired up or at odds with a Wall Street Journal reporter (the wonderful Amy Ryan, who admittedly doesn't have a lot to do in this film) who has been reporting on the confirmation of the WMD in Iraq, the top CIA man in Iraq (a terrific Brendan Gleeson), and the two-faced face of the DOD for the Administration in Iraq (played with force and conviction by Greg Kinnear). As the hunt for Magellan becomes more intense, so does the effort to stop Miller before he gets too close to the truth (represented by an unrecognizable Jason Isaacs as a mega-tough Special Forces operative).<br /><br />Before you start to think that because Greengrass and Damon have reunited for a film that this is \\"Jason Bourne in Iraq\\", you'd be dead wrong. Roy Miller couldn't be more different than Jason Bourne. They are both men of action who are on a quest for facts and that's where the similarities end. Damon is a great actor, and he turns in another great performance here. Greengrass is a tremendously gifted director with a real eye for pacing and putting the audience in the thick of the events and action in his films. Speaking of which, can we stop whining about his \\"shaky-cam\\" action style? It works. It's intense. It won't make you throw up. End of story. The script by the great Brian Helgeland, who has scripted so many terrific films like L.A. CONFIDENTIAL, CONSPIRACY THEORY (severely underrated), MAN ON FIRE, MYSTIC RIVER (and also happens to be a very good director in his own right with A KNIGHT'S TALE, THE ORDER and PAYBACK), also turns in a tight and real script here.<br /><br />There isn't really a false move in this whole film, and it explores a fundamental flaw to something that shouldn't be ignored.<br /><br />The interesting part of this film is that it is based somewhat in fact. The character of Roy Miller is based on a real Warrant Officer who was asking many of the same questions that Miller asks. Obviously there's some dramatic license taken here, but still... why we go to war is as important as the lives that are lost during that war.<br /><br />In regards to the Blu-Ray disc, the supplemental material is pretty great and the transfer looks and sounds terrific, so I'm not sure why there have been complaints to the transfer.<br /><br />All in all, Greengrass and Damon bring us another intensely satisfying film experience, and whatever your beliefs about the Iraq war, this is a film worth viewing.so I'm not sure why there have been complaints to the transfer.
